Vice President JD Vance Delivers Remarks in Budapest, Hungary

The White House(3.1M) ·67:02 ·42.8K views · 2026-04-07
JD Vance (Vice President of the United States)
Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán celebrated a "golden age" of U.S.-Hungarian relations in Budapest, framing their alliance as a shared defense of national sovereignty, traditional family values, and Western civilization against...
TL;DR Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán celebrated a "golden age" of U.S.-Hungarian relations in Budapest, framing their alliance as a shared defense of national sovereignty, traditional family values, and Western civilization against the "globalist"...

TL;DR

Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán celebrated a "golden age" of U.S.-Hungarian relations in Budapest, framing their alliance as a shared defense of national sovereignty, traditional family values, and Western civilization against the "globalist" influence of the Brussels-based European Union.

A "Golden Age" of U.S.-Hungarian Relations

  • Strategic Partnership: Both leaders highlighted the unprecedented alignment between the Trump administration and the Orbán government, characterized by shared political and economic goals.
      • Trump Endorsement: Former President Donald Trump participated via a live phone call, praising Orbán for refusing to allow Hungary to be "invaded" by migrants and endorsing his leadership as a model for strong nations.
      • Vance’s Mission: VP JD Vance explicitly stated he was sent by Donald Trump to stand with Orbán, affirming that the U.S. supports Hungary’s right to prioritize its own people over international mandates.
  • Economic Patriotism: The speakers advocated for an "economic patriotism" that protects domestic jobs and brings industry back home, arguing that globalization should not be an end in itself.

Defense of National Sovereignty and Western Civilization

  • The "Brussels" Conflict: Orbán and Vance characterized the European Union leadership in Brussels as a "progressive elite" that seeks to strip nations of their independence through migration mandates and "woke" ideology.
      • Internal Enemies: Vance argued that Western civilization is not threatened by external enemies but by internal "radicals" who manage national decline rather than seeking renewal.
      • Sovereignty as a Solution: Hungary was presented as a "cornerstone of independence" that proves a nation can secure its borders and prioritize its workers without becoming isolated.
  • Civilizational Pillars: The speakers identified the foundations of their friendship as "God, Family, and Homeland."
      • Religious Heritage: Vance cited the "sacrificial love of Jesus Christ" and the laws of Moses as the roots of free and prosperous societies.

Geopolitics and the War in Ukraine

  • Anti-Sanction Stance: Prime Minister Orbán delivered a sharp critique of EU sanctions against Russia, calling them "suicide" for the European economy and blaming them for skyrocketing energy prices.
  • Opposition to Escalation: Orbán accused Brussels of wanting to send European youth to the "eastern front" and expressed frustration over the oil blockade and the blowing up of the Nord Stream pipeline.
  • Peace Through Strength: The leaders emphasized a desire to "close the Russian-Ukrainian war" and pivot away from what they described as the self-destructive policies of the current European leadership.

Historical Ties and Shared Destiny

  • Historical Heroes: Both speakers referenced historical figures who bridged the two nations, including:
      • Mihály Kováts: A Hungarian hussar who organized the U.S. Continental Army’s cavalry.
      • Lajos Kossuth: The Hungarian democracy leader who was famously welcomed in Vance’s home state of Ohio in the 19th century.
      • Ronald Reagan: Praised by Orbán for his role in ending Soviet occupation and liberating Hungary.
  • 2026 Election Stakes: Vance framed the upcoming Hungarian elections as a choice between national "resurrection" and becoming "insignificant" under globalist rule, urging voters to maintain the current path of freedom and security.

If they don't believe in the future, why do they want a life in politics? Yet they speak not of renewal for our nations, but management. They're not trying to build a great future; they're trying to manage the decline of the greatest civilization in the world. Some of them say things like human beings are no more than pollution upon the earth. They look at our cultures and our borders, they look at the very idea of a nation and ask how we can get rid of them. Every position, I believe, flows from this fundamental error. They reject mothers and motherhood, fathers and fatherhood in the name of liberation. They condemn children to mutilation and sterilization in the name of gender care. And they practice institutional murder in the name of quote, end of life planning. And if you dare speak up about it, they will fight using the modern tools of social media to silence you through censorship. We understand that we have a sacred duty to protect life, to defend the value of our people's hard work, to invest in our workers, our families and our industry. And to make it easier to build a life that is affordable for all of our citizens. We are committed to our future because we are committed to the very idea of our people. We're committed to the idea of life itself, because it is a gift from God and we never forget it. Now, that's why I'm here. That's why I'm here, ladies and gentlemen, that's why President Trump sent me to stand here with Viktor today, something I'm very proud to do. Because I believe our nations are incredibly capable of greatness when we come together. Our work is not zero-sum; indeed it cannot be because our goal is always to build a better life for our people. These bureaucrats, they've given us a false choice. Think about this: they tell us that the options are between isolation and globalist integration. They have framed their project as the inevitable future, even as their very institutions stagnate and crumble. But we know there's a better way: cooperation between countries with shared values and parallel destinies. That is the story of Hungary and America and we're going to keep fighting for it. A lot of you may not know this, but this is the story of a much longer Hungarian-American friendship. When my own country sought its independence 250 years ago, almost to the month, it was a Hungarian soldier by the name of Michael Kováts who helped found the first American cavalry units, ultimately giving his life in our struggle for independence against the British Empire. A generation later, Americans welcomed Louis Kossuth, the hero of 1848 and the father of Hungarian democracy. Kossuth was greeted in the United States like a rock star, much better than a politician. His arrival and the more general cause of Hungarian independence captured the imagination of our young nation. He received the distinction, the second foreigner ever in our nation's history after Lafayette, to address a joint meeting of Congress and his bust stands in the United States Capitol to this very day. Now during that trip, I didn't realize this until a few days ago, but during that trip to the United States, Kossuth visited my home state of Ohio to make his case for Hungarian independence. We have some Ohio fans over here, that's good. Before the state legislature in Columbus, Ohio, he declared: quote, the spirit of our age is democracy, all for the people and all by the people. Nothing about the people without the people. My nation will rise, called the resurrection by the eternal principles of the law of nature and of nature's God. Even then, this great Hungarian patriot was aware of the intimate link between sovereignty, between self-government and between our divine creator. And I'm proud to say that according to the history books, the part of the country that gave him the proudest reception and the biggest reception during his entire time in America was my hometown of Cincinnati, Ohio. You could imagine this and you tell these stories and you think: how can the bureaucrats think that we are not capable of self-government and choosing our own destiny? Because when Kossuth came to Cincinnati during his tour of Ohio, there were railroad tracks lined with citizens delighted to behold Hungary's great freedom fighter. Reportedly, 100,000 of them showed up just at his one stop in my hometown. And the affection, I got to say, I'm a little biased here, the affection was mutual. The people of Cincinnati, Kossuth said: quote, change wilderness of primitive forests into an immense city, of which there exists a prediction that by the year of our Lord 2000, it will be the greatest city in the world. And no offense to Budapest, but I think he was right about that. But it tells you something very real that when Kossuth looked at the United States of America, he didn't see something radically different; he saw something familiar. In our nation he recognized the same forces at work that were shaping Hungary. People building something of their own out of wilderness with purpose, conviction, and a deep belief in where they came from and what they were called to do. And standing in Cincinnati, he saw something in America that he believed was just the beginning. The West, the West, he exclaimed, there you can see the cradle of a newborn humanity. It was true then and it's still true today. But America, like Hungary, was not a place just of rest. It was built around the idea of creating and renewing. And those early Americans, like the heroes of your own nation, took that inheritance and they shaped it into their own. They added to it. They fortified it. They passed it down to their children and to their grandchildren who then did the same, with the expectation that generations later, those grandchildren would carry it forward. On his fateful trip to America, Kossuth announced that Hungary was to become—and this is perhaps my favorite quote—the cornerstone of national independence on the European continent. This guy was a prophet. Kossuth called this the cornerstone of independence, the cornerstone of sovereignty on the European continent and though he didn't live to see it become so, I declare that prophecy is true today in 2026. Now, under Viktor Orbán's leadership, you have held on to the civilizational goods that make a country worth living in in the first place. Sovereignty, prosperity, history, a sense of national community, the redemptive nature of bringing new life and new families into the world. This is an awesome and difficult responsibility. Because in much of the West, there's a growing uncertainty about whether these things matter or whether they're worth fighting for. But not here. You have stood up to the bureaucrats, you have stood up to the nihilists and now I wonder, will you do it again? Will you stand against the bureaucrats in Brussels? Will you stand for sovereignty and democracy? Will you stand for Western civilization? Will you stand for freedom, for truth, and for the God of our fathers? Then my friends, go to the polls in the weekend, stand with Viktor Orbán because he stands for you and he stands for all these things. God bless Hungary and God bless the United States of America. Thank you.

Jamie Dimon cautions that Iran war “increases the odds of bad economic outcomes”

NPR(798.0K) ·31:06 ·16.2K views · 2026-04-07
Jamie Dimon (CEO, JPMorgan Chase)
JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that escalating geopolitical tensions, particularly involving Iran, and unsustainable U.S.
TL;DR JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that escalating geopolitical tensions, particularly involving Iran, and unsustainable U.S. federal deficits increase the likelihood of "bad economic outcomes" like stagflation. He advocates for a "civic-minded" corporate strategy that...

TL;DR

JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that escalating geopolitical tensions, particularly involving Iran, and unsustainable U.S. federal deficits increase the likelihood of "bad economic outcomes" like stagflation. He advocates for a "civic-minded" corporate strategy that prioritizes skills-based education, AI-driven productivity, and expanded tax credits to preserve the American Dream.

Geopolitical Instability and Global Security

  • The Iran Threat: Dimon identifies Iran as a critical risk to global democracy and "mankind," citing its 47-year history of aggression, ballistic missile capabilities, and pursuit of nuclear weapons.
      • Economic "Blast Radius": While Dimon avoids predicting a specific timeline, he notes that conflict increases the odds of recession, inflation, or stagflation.
      • Energy Security: The "worst-case scenario" involves losing control of the Straits of Hormuz, which would send oil and gas prices soaring globally.
  • Global Alliances: He emphasizes that the U.S. must lead in keeping the world "safe for democracy," facing challenges from a coalition including Ukraine, Iran, North Korea, and China.

U.S. Fiscal Health and Market Confidence

  • The Federal Deficit: Dimon warns that the U.S. budget deficit—currently at 6% of GDP—will eventually trigger a crisis characterized by volatile markets and "bond vigilantes" refusing to buy U.S. Treasuries.
      • The 3% Growth Target: He argues that the deficit problem can be managed if the U.S. achieves 3% annual GDP growth through better policy in education, immigration, and smarter regulation.
  • Investment Safe Haven: Despite fiscal concerns, Dimon maintains that the U.S. remains the world's premier investment destination due to its geography, military, rule of law, and innovative culture.
  • Interest Rate Pressures: Rising rates on U.S. Treasury bonds are attributed to persistent inflationary pressures from deficit spending and global energy costs.

AI and the Evolution of the Workforce

  • Industrial Transformation: Dimon compares the current AI investment boom (with "hyperscalers" borrowing $750 billion this year) to the historical impacts of electricity, the internal combustion engine, and the internet.
  • The 3.5-Day Work Week: He predicts that AI-driven productivity could eventually reduce the standard work week to three and a half days for future generations.
  • Labor Redeployment: Rather than mass unemployment, Dimon envisions a shift in job roles.
      • Corporate Responsibility: He advocates for "redeployment," retraining, and income assistance for workers displaced by technology.
      • Positive Externalities: Beyond efficiency, AI is expected to contribute to breakthroughs in cancer research, climate solutions, and transportation safety.

Domestic Policy and "The American Dream"

  • Urban Competitiveness: Dimon notes that JPMorgan now has more employees in Texas than New York. He warns that high-tax cities like New York risk driving away talent and capital if they do not remain "hospitable" to business.
  • Educational Reform: He proposes that high schools and community colleges be measured by "outcomes"—specifically the wages and jobs graduates secure.
      • Model: He cites vocational programs, like aviation maintenance, where 17-year-olds can graduate into $75,000+ per year careers.
  • Expanding the Safety Net: Dimon strongly advocates for doubling the Earned Income Tax Credit (EITC) and removing the child requirement, calling it a "home run" for incentivizing work and reducing crime and recidivism.

"I think if we had good policy... we can grow 3%. We should aspire to 3%. We can do probably even better than that. This is the most innovative nation the world has ever seen." — Jamie Dimon
"I do think that there’s a good chance [the work week] to be three and a half days a week... in many years they’ll be living wonderful lives." — Jamie Dimon
"When they said the pursuit of happiness, they didn’t mean happiness like we mean happiness—'do you feel good?' They meant purpose." — Jamie Dimon
Jamie Dimon is the CEO of JPMorgan Chase, this nation’s largest bank. He’s also connected to many of the wealthy and powerful in New York and here in Washington, where we spoke with Dimon in the JPMorgan offices on the occasion of an annual letter in which he gives his opinions about almost everything. Thanks for welcoming us here. It’s good to be here. Thank you. Thank you for coming here. And I read your letter. It’s really compelling. Read the whole thing? Just—yeah, absolutely. Every page. It is more interesting than the average corporate document because you have opinions on many topics. And that’s my first question. Why do you feel you should, as a CEO, be speaking out on topics all across the news when you probably could stay silent? Yeah. So it’s very important. So I, when I do these letters, I think to myself what’s important to the company, what’s important to employees, what’s important to our shareholders. I actually make a list of questions, talk to people, I want to answer the big important questions. And the things you’re asking about, most of it’s about the company, but the last section, which is about America and the world, I always say it’s predicated upon the fact that if America doesn’t do well, JPMorgan will have a real hard time doing well. And that we have a deep interest in that. And the second reason is that, you know, policy—you can't—I’m not saying that government can’t do it—we shouldn’t rely on government alone. Collaboration works. Okay? Collaboration worked in Detroit, it worked in World War II, it worked in all these things. So I think it’s good for business to get involved, to bring their expertise to bear to help all the citizens of this country. And that helps the country and your company. Do you assume that the interests of the country are about the same as the interests of your company? No. But I think that we have common interests. So that, you know, we all—if all of our citizens do better, we’ll all do better. I think a lot of people come to Washington, tons of special interest groups, I think there are like 17,000 lobbying organizations, and they all fight for their own stuff. I’m kind of more in the camp that we should also fight for what’s good for the country. If the country grew faster, we’d all be better off. And you—people talk about polarization and things that don’t work. I also think it is our job to lift up all our citizens. That is what we should do. We should be civic-minded, not just, you know, about our—ourselves. And so—and banks have been doing that for years. If you go to—actually, a lot of companies have been doing that for years as part of just the normal culture. Sometimes it’s local, sometimes it’s national. The Business Roundtable here gets involved in public policy that’s good for the country, not the public policy that’s good for banks or private equity or chemical companies or pharmaceutical companies or movie companies. And I think we need to do more of that. What’s good for the country. One of many things you comment on is the war in Iran. You talk about geopolitical risk. It’s right up there. I know that you’ve said in recent days that you approve generally of the idea of the war to attack a threat in Iran. I’d like to know, though, what you think of the president’s leadership in the war and particularly his recent threats to bomb Iran back to the Stone Age, to use his words. Well, I’m—I’m not going to comment on that. But—but I mean—I mean I want to put this in a broader context. The most important thing that we can do is make sure that the world is safe for democracy. And it’s being challenged today in Ukraine, Iran, North Korea, somewhat by China. I think that is probably the most critical issue. What world are we going to have the next 40 or 50 years? This is a part of that. So I’m not—I was not supporting and not supporting. What I pointed out in my letter is, you know, people talked about being an imminent threat. It’s not a threat. They’ve been killing and murdering innocent people, including innocent Americans, you know, for 47 years. They have missiles—and ballistic missiles that can go 3,000 miles, and they clearly are trying to develop nuclear capability. I agree with the concept they can’t be allowed to have nuclear capability. And so that’s where I’m saying, I’m not an expert in it. I don’t know all the choices they have. I know the military is exceptional. I don’t know what their plan B, their plan C is. I’m simply pointing out that it—it’s—you gotta look at that risk as being an enormous risk for mankind. And so—so I want—I hope we prevail. And—so—and I know it causes other problems in society and, you know, the cost of fuel, the cost of oil. I complete—I completely understand that and I’m quite sympathetic to that. But this is a really important subject that has to be properly dealt with eventually. What are the economic risks, which is your area of expertise, of the potential destruction of this war? As we’re talking, the president has just had a press conference and talked about destroying Iranian power plants. The Iranians have talked about destroying infrastructure in response. The economic blast radius could even be bigger than it has been. Yeah. No. So again, I’m separating morality from—you talk about economics. I think the morality may be more important than—free and safe world may be more important. And that’s hard to understand. You know, we did that in World War II. You could pay tremendous sacrifices. But economically, you know, there’s tons of uncertainty. And I list like tons of them out there, not just these wars. But obviously, they can cause help—cause—they usually ends up in some form of recession. You know, recession is unemployment, it could be stagflation, inflation, recession, which are the worst. It could be, you know, where it pushes inflation down. It could be short. I don’t know. It may not happen at all. So I’m not even saying it’s going to happen. I just think it increases the odds of bad economic outcomes. And we should just be clear-eyed about that. Is—to be clear-eyed, is there some way to measure the economic damage of this war so far? I think the—best way to look at it so far is that, you know, people here, you know, are paying more for gas and might end up paying more for food and——but if ends up in the right place, you know, you gotta look at that quite carefully. So I—I don’t know yet. You don’t know yet. I don’t know yet. Do you have in mind a worst-case scenario and a best-case scenario? Yeah, I think the worst case is that somehow we don’t get control of the Straits of Hormuz, that—that we have to back out, that oil and gas that—Iran doesn’t give up and oil and gas price goes even higher today. That’s probably the worst-case scenario. And the best case is that they—that they negotiate something where they don’t build nuclear weapons, the Straits of Hormuz is opened up, and we go back to a more peaceful world. Listening to your worst case, I think I hear you saying as a citizen, the United States has to win this, that losing it would be— I—I don’t want to go that far because you’re—that’s putting words in my mouth. I don’t know what all the potential outcomes are and neither do you. Okay? So— Fair enough. Yeah. And—and we all—after the fact, we’ll be having strong opinions in hindsight. And even hindsight is not perfect. I say even in hindsight you don’t know history. I point out in my letter that we’re still analyzing what happened in World War I. Without a doubt. Right. Without a doubt. There’s a thing that’s happening in real time that’s particularly interesting and that relates to the financial markets. The president regularly has made statements about this war and other issues that have moved the markets. Now, that’s normal. You’ve been around a long time. Every president moves the markets. But they’ve been quite sudden, quite frequent, quite dramatic. And sometimes there is news suggesting that someone profited in the moments when that happened. What do you think about when you watch that? I—look, I have to deal with the world I got, so I’m—I don’t spend that much time worrying about it. I think if people are profiting, that’s bad. I think, you know, when the president changes his mind, I don’t think that’s always a bad thing. You know, he wants to do X, it doesn’t work that well, he tries something different. That’s okay. You know, not mandate it, you know, let the system work. The system will adjust eventually. And as—you could say that, you know, in Europe they’re already working four days a week. What do you think about when someone says, on NPR as they did the other day, one of the risks here, one of the goals here is to replace almost everybody’s job? Well, I don’t—I don’t like that. I don’t think that’s going to happen. And there are a lot of jobs that are not replaceable, and you’re going to wake up in the morning, you’re still going to have to eat something and go somewhere and go hiking and talk to people and need shrinks and all—there are tons of jobs. I mean I just—and even to build these data centers, you’re talking about tons of labor, engineers, people who are building the stuff, cement, steel, servers. So there is a lot of jobs. They’re building whole towns next to new data centers. Whole towns. And this—this will adjust over time. The real question, if it goes too fast, to have the adjustment we had in prior large technological advances. That’s the real question. And we should start to really think about what society should do to deal with that if it happens. Is AI going to eliminate a lot of entry-level jobs? I don’t know yet. I—I don’t know yet, because we’re still going to need people who bank clients. So it—you know, what it may very well do is change what that entry-level job is. You know, a lot of those entry-level jobs are a lot of paperwork that’ll be eliminated. And you can say, well, then you can do it with less people. Maybe, but I also need those people to call on clients, so that job may change. You know, the job may—IBM is doing something really neat. They’re hiring as many young people, but a lot more of them are AI experts. Hm. They’ve been using AI kind of the—AI native, they started with AI. So there may be jobs that we’re doing so they can train people and one day they can go, you know, be the client exec, you know, covering a—a large global client. Is something like that happening at JPMorgan? A little bit. We’ve always done what I call redeployment. You know, we’ve always been tak—you know, jobs are going up and going down, we always say, hey, Steve, we really like you, you know, here’s some a whole bunch of other jobs. You know, sometimes there’s no fit or you don’t want to, you want to retire. But other times, yeah, we retrain you, move to another job. So, you know, there are people in our branches who are in the mortgage business. There are people in the mortgage business who used to be in the branches. There are people who want to do different things, and so one of the things that JPMorgan could do is offer you great opportunities in life. You know, in—in the United States, sometimes around the world, and I think people—the next generation will probably have a lot more jobs, changes in their career than we’ve had in ours. There is a line in your letter that I want to try to decipher for someone like me. I think you’re telling me that asset prices, things like stocks and real estate and so forth, are grossly overpriced. The actual language is that they’re more valuable relative to the economy than they were before the 2008 financial crisis. What's happening? Yeah. The 50-State Plan: Public-Private Models for AI Infrastructure and University Transformation

NVIDIA(2.2M) ·36:50 ·172 views · 2026-04-07
NVIDIA is democratizing AI education through its Deep Learning Institute (DLI) by providing universities with free, industry-standard curriculum kits and a certified "Ambassador" program, bridging the gap between academic theory and high-performance computing (HPC) career readiness.
TL;DR NVIDIA is democratizing AI education through its Deep Learning Institute (DLI) by providing universities with free, industry-standard curriculum kits and a certified "Ambassador" program, bridging the gap between academic theory and high-performance computing (HPC)...

TL;DR

NVIDIA is democratizing AI education through its Deep Learning Institute (DLI) by providing universities with free, industry-standard curriculum kits and a certified "Ambassador" program, bridging the gap between academic theory and high-performance computing (HPC) career readiness.

The Deep Learning Institute (DLI) Ecosystem

The DLI serves as a centralized hub for high-performance computing education, focusing on practical, hands-on experience rather than theoretical lectures.

  • Hands-on Infrastructure: All courses run on the DLI platform, an Open edX-based system that provides students with cloud access to real NVIDIA GPUs, eliminating the need for universities to configure complex local lab environments.
  • Industry-Recognized Credentials: Learners earn unique, traceable certificates upon passing assessments. These are designed to be "career-building" assets for LinkedIn and resumes.
  • Breadth of Content: The catalog spans from fundamentals like Deep Learning and Python-based modeling to advanced topics such as:
      • Generative AI: Large Language Models (LLMs) and Diffusion Models.
      • Physical AI: Robotics, OpenUSD for 3D simulation, and Edge computing (Jetson Orin Nano).
      • Accelerated Computing: Using CUDA for domain science and RAPIDS for data science.

The DLI Ambassador Program: Empowering Faculty

This "high-touch" program transforms faculty into NVIDIA-certified instructors, allowing them to deliver specialized workshops on campus or at conferences.

  • Vetting and Certification: Applicants (primarily faculty or HPC staff) must undergo a technical review and a formal interview with an NVIDIA expert to ensure instructional quality.
  • Financial and Logistics Support:
      • Event Support: NVIDIA provides up to $500 in reimbursement for catering to help attract students to workshops.
      • Travel Grants: Support is available for instructors teaching at other universities or academic conferences.
      • Enterprise Opportunities: Ambassadors can purchase workshops at a discount to resell to enterprise clients for profit.
  • Exclusive Access: There are currently fewer than 1,000 Ambassadors worldwide. They receive early access to new workshops before they are released as self-paced versions.

Teaching Kits: Modular Curriculum for Higher Ed

For institutions seeking a "lower-touch" entry point, NVIDIA offers downloadable Teaching Kits designed for full-semester integration.

  • Comprehensive Resources: Kits include lecture slides, videos, Jupyter notebooks (optimized for Google Colab), and problem sets.
  • Flexible Licensing: Content is released under a non-commercial Creative Commons license, allowing educators to "pick and choose" modules to fit existing courses.
  • Specific Domain Kits:
      • GenAI & OpenUSD: The latest kits include prep material for professional certification exams.
      • Accelerated Data Science: Co-developed with Georgia Tech and Prairie View A&M.
      • Deep Learning for Science: Focuses on Physics-ML for fluid dynamics and biomedicine.

Case Study: Career-Focused AI at ECPI University

Professor Paul Nussbaum shared results from integrating DLI workshops into ECPI’s accelerated, career-focused curriculum.

  • High Student Demand: Despite being voluntary 8-hour sessions held outside of class hours (often on Fridays), workshops regularly reach 100-student capacity.
  • Interdisciplinary Application: AI is being taught across silos, including showing culinary students how AI can assist in recipe generation and plating imagery.
  • Tangible Career Outcomes:
      • Skill Validation: Nussbaum notes a ~70% pass rate, ensuring the certificate remains a rigorous proof of skill.
      • Professional Growth: Students have cited these certifications as the primary reason for master's program admissions and promotions to AI lead roles in industry.

Notable Quotes

"Educators using this course don't need to configure anything in their labs. It's all taken care of by NVIDIA... you’re driving a Ferrari. NVIDIA provides the GPUs, and boy, is it zippy." — Joe Bungo
"I tell students: this is not a lean-back webinar. This is a lean-forwards, hands-on workshop where you’ve got to modify code, read code, and train models." — Paul Nussbaum
"We feel that AI is going to impact every future career. That’s why we take a holistic approach—from electronics engineering to business and even culinary arts." — Paul Nussbaum

Vice President JD Vance Delivers Remarks with Prime Minister Viktor Orbán of Hungary

The White House(3.1M) ·34:00 ·54.2K views · 2026-04-07
JD Vance (Vice President, United States) Viktor Orbán (Prime Minister, Hungary)
Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán met in Budapest to affirm a "Golden Era" of U.S.-Hungary relations, centered on a shared "moral cooperation" to defend Western civilization, achieve energy independence, and broker a diplomatic end to the war in Ukraine.
TL;DR Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán met in Budapest to affirm a "Golden Era" of U.S.-Hungary relations, centered on a shared "moral cooperation" to defend Western civilization, achieve energy independence, and broker a diplomatic end to the war in...

TL;DR

Vice President JD Vance and Prime Minister Viktor Orbán met in Budapest to affirm a "Golden Era" of U.S.-Hungary relations, centered on a shared "moral cooperation" to defend Western civilization, achieve energy independence, and broker a diplomatic end to the war in Ukraine.

Strategic Economic and Energy Cooperation

  • Record Growth: Prime Minister Orbán identified 2025 as a record year for bilateral relations, noting a 50% increase in trade turnover and 100 billion Hungarian Forints in FDI from 30 American companies.
  • Energy Security Model: Vice President Vance praised Orbán as Europe’s most "profound leader" on energy, arguing that Hungary’s lower utility prices prove that Orbán’s policies should have been the model for the rest of the continent.
  • Pipeline Blockades: Orbán reported that Ukraine has blockaded the "umbilical cord" of the Hungarian economy—the oil and gas pipelines from Russia.
      • Political Motivation: Orbán alleged these blockades were timed to influence the upcoming Hungarian election in hopes of installing a pro-Ukrainian government.
  • Technological Expansion: Cooperation has expanded beyond traditional trade into high-tech sectors, including space technology, defense, and artificial intelligence.

Diplomacy and the Ukraine-Russia Conflict

  • Budapest Peace Summit: Prime Minister Orbán offered Budapest as the host venue for a potential peace summit between the U.S. and Russia, noting that technical preparations have already been discussed with both Washington and Moscow.
  • Failure of European Strategy: Orbán argued that the European/Brussels strategy of weakening Russia through economic warfare has failed because Russia possesses unlimited raw materials while Europe does not.
  • Shared Peace Effort: Both leaders asserted that the war would never have started if Donald Trump were President and criticized "chest-beating" politicians in Brussels for blocking diplomatic resolutions.
      • Human Cost: Orbán highlighted that ethnic Hungarians living in Ukraine are being drafted and killed in the conflict, making peace a direct national interest for Hungary.

Defense of Western Civilization and Sovereignty

  • Moral Alignment: Vance characterized the relationship not just as economic, but as "moral cooperation" based on shared Christian values, the rule of law, and the protection of the family unit.
  • Ideological Priorities: The leaders identified four key areas of continuous exchange:
      • Migration: Maintaining border integrity.
      • Gender Ideology: Opposing "indoctrination" in schools.
      • Family Policy: Supporting traditional domestic structures.
      • Global Security: Leveraging Hungary’s network in Eastern Europe and the Balkans.
  • Foreign Interference: Vance and Orbán both condemned "disgraceful" interference from Brussels bureaucrats and foreign security services in Hungarian elections, including digital censorship and financial pressure.

Global Security: Iran and Middle East Tensions

  • U.S. Deadline for Iran: Vice President Vance confirmed a deadline (8:00 PM U.S. time) for Iran to reach a diplomatic deal or face "much greater economic cost," including potential strikes on infrastructure.
  • Military Objectives: Vance stated that the U.S. has largely accomplished its military objectives regarding Iran's manufacturing capabilities; the current focus is on stopping Iranian "economic terrorism" in the Strait of Hormuz.
  • Two Pathways for Tehran: Vance outlined two options for Iran:
      • Pathway A: Becoming a "normal country" that participates in global commerce and stops funding terrorism.
      • Pathway B: Continued economic isolation and potential infrastructure destruction if they refuse to negotiate.
"I’m not here primarily because of the economic cooperation... I’m here because of the moral cooperation... the defense of the idea that children should be able to go to school and get educated and not indoctrinated." — Vice President JD Vance
"To wage an economic war against a country that has unlimited energy resources and raw materials while those waging the economic war do not have energy... was a very strange idea." — Prime Minister Viktor Orbán
"Viktor Orbán has been the single most profound leader in Europe on the question of energy security and independence... it is funny to watch Prime Ministers in some Western European capitals talk about the energy crisis when they should have been following the policies of Viktor Orbán." — Vice President JD Vance
"Hungary remains ready so that if the US and Russia believe that a peace summit is required between the two of them, then Budapest will be happy to provide itself as a venue." — Prime Minister Viktor Orbán
Good afternoon, ladies and gentlemen. Good afternoon, ladies and gentlemen. I'd like to respectfully welcome you all and I'd like to especially welcome his Excellency JD Vance, the 50th Vice President of the United States of America, at this press conference on the occasion of his visit to Hungary. I'd like to welcome Prime Minister Viktor Orbán and Hungarian and American delegation members. I'd like to ask Prime Minister Viktor Orbán to deliver his statement. Good afternoon, ladies and gentlemen. If you'll allow me, I'm going to speak in my mother tongue, Hungarian. I'd like to respectfully and cordially welcome Vice President Vance to Hungary. The last time a Vice President from the US visited Hungary was 35 years ago and we haven't had such a high-ranked American dignitary in Hungary for 20 years. And 20 years, that's quite a long period of time. With the election of President Trump, I believe a golden era has been ushered in in our relations. We have enumerated the—the year of records was 2025 in terms of economic cooperation. 2026 also is increasing impetus. We have increased our turnover by 50% and we had 30 American companies announce FDI to the tune of 100 billion Hungarian Forints. We've also strengthened our cooperation, expanded it with space technology and defense. We owe gratitude to President Trump and Vice President Vance for standing by Hungary during the past years. The United States of America is the strongest country in the world and I am happy to say that they are our allies today. The peace and the security of Hungary, therefore, is guaranteed. Ladies and gentlemen, we also discussed the fact that Europe is heading towards one of the worst energy crises of all times. We are seeing drastic price hikes and if we do not take measures on time, we are going to see a shortage of energy, oil, and gas. In this situation, it is especially important that we have the energy cooperation between the US and Hungary without which we would not be able to guarantee the—the energy needs of Hungary and we could not cap our utility prices. We've talked about the United States' efforts to achieve peace. Hungary has always supported the US and President Trump personally in this peace effort. We've been living in the shadows of a war for four years now and we are convinced that if President Trump were the president in 2022, there would not be a war now. It would not have started. And if the Europeans, especially Brussels, would not be blocking the peace efforts of the president, peace would prevail, would have been reinstated in Ukraine for a long time already. I've also explained to the Vice President that Hungary is experiencing very, very, very harsh and very open interference by foreign security services into our elections. This is why we especially welcome the decisions of the President of the United States of America with which he has—he has closed the financial taps that supported interference into the elections of other countries. I've been waiting for a long, long time for this meeting and I'm very grateful that we met today. I am grateful that we were able to discuss with the Vice President the pressing issues, the great issues of Western civilization. I am not sharing any secret when I say that there is a continuous discussion between us, an exchange of experiences related to government work, especially in four areas. One, migration; number two, gender ideology; number three, family policy; and number four, global security. Because in these areas, fields, Hungary has amassed substantial experiences and quite an extended network of contacts in Eastern Europe and the Balkans. As a result of our discussions today, we have agreed that it is in the interest of both parties to continue this cooperation and that the strategic cooperation between the two countries is going to be continuous and will be continued. Thank you very much for honoring us with your presence, for coming to Hungary. Prime Minister, thank you very much and now I ask JD Vance to deliver his statement. Well, thank you Prime Minister first of all, and thanks to the people of Hungary for welcoming me. This is a beautiful city, a city that I've been to once before on a personal trip, probably five or six years ago. I remember the first time that I came to this beautiful country, my wife was about 20 weeks pregnant with our second child. And now we've come back to Budapest and my wife is 20 weeks pregnant with our fourth child. So there's an interesting—interesting way in which our trips to Hungary have rhymed. I also want to thank the President of the United States, who of course is a dear friend of Prime Minister Orbán and a very strident supporter of Prime Minister Orbán because together the President of the United States and the Prime Minister of Hungary have been able to do amazing things. And we're here because we want to celebrate those amazing things, we want to build upon those amazing things, and of course I want to help as much as I possibly can the Prime Minister as he faces this—this election season, which I believe is happening in just about a week, the election to—to elect the next Prime Minister of Hungary. Now I don't expect of course the people of Hungary to listen to the Vice President of the United States. That's not primarily why I'm here. But I—I did want to send a signal to everybody, particularly the bureaucrats in Brussels who have done everything that they can to hold down the people of Hungary because they don't like the leader who has actually stood up for the people of Hungary. And I think it's important to say that. There are so many things that we could point to, there are so many economic pieces of cooperation, so much investment that's come into Hungary from the United States. I think Viktor Orbán has been the single most profound leader in Europe on the question of energy—energy security and independence. It is funny to watch Prime Ministers and leaders in some of the Western European capitals talk about the energy crisis when frankly they should have been following the policies of Viktor Orbán in Hungary. And if they had, the energy crisis that they're experiencing would be a lot less bad because what's going on in Hungary right now is that while yes, energy prices are elevated, they are far less elevated here than they are almost anywhere else in Europe. And that's because of the leadership of the man who's standing next to me. And I think that leadership can provide a model to the continent. We want Europe to be successful. We want European families to be able to afford to heat their homes and to build great things. We want Europe to be energy independent and even energy dominant, but it's not going to be energy secure if it continues to follow the failed policies of the past. And so I think Viktor has been a great example in charting a course that could lead to a better, more prosperous, and more energy-secure Europe. There's a lot of other cooperation in technology and artificial intelligence and manufacturing. There are so many ways in which the United States and Hungary have been great economic partners and that partnership has really accelerated over the past couple of years under President Trump's leadership. But ladies and gentlemen, I'm not here primarily, Viktor, because of the economic cooperation between our countries. I'm here because of the moral cooperation between our two countries. Because what the United States and Hungary together represent under Viktor's leadership and under President Trump's leadership is the defense of Western civilization. The defense of the idea that children should be able to go to school and get educated and not indoctrinated. The defense of the idea that European and American families should be able to transport themselves and be able to afford to heat and cool their homes. The defense of the idea that—that we are founded on a certain Christian civilization and Christian values that animate everything from freedom of speech to rule of law to respect for minority rights and protection of the vulnerable. There is so much that unites the United States and Hungary and unfortunately there have been too few people who have been willing to stand up for the values of Western civilization. Viktor Orbán is the rare exception that has unfortunately proved the rule. That's one of the reasons why I'm here. I'm here because Viktor is a statesman. And we have seen so much talk in European capitals about the need to end the war in Russia and Ukraine and we certainly agree with it. The war would have never started under President—if President Trump had been president four years ago, but now that it has started, probably the two leaders who have done the most to actually end that destructive conflict have been Donald J. Trump and Viktor Orbán in Hungary. And they've done it through diplomacy, through talking to people, through trying to understand what the Ukrainians and the Russians need to end the war. We're going to continue to participate in that process, but I think that it is a testament to the people of Hungary that you're a country of 10 million people, but I'm telling you, I've sat in all the rooms and I've been on all the phone calls, your leadership has been a far, far more important and constructive partner for peace than almost anyone anywhere else in the world. And that is a great testament I think to the—to the wisdom and the courage of the people of Hungary. And then finally, just want to say something, one final observation about—about this election. What has happened in this country, what has happened in the—in the midst of this election campaign is one of the worst examples of foreign intellectual interference that I've ever seen or ever even read about. The bureaucrats in Brussels have tried to destroy the economy of Hungary. They have tried to make Hungary less energy independent. They have tried to drive up costs for Hungarian consumers. And they've done it all because they hate this guy. But I think that what the people of Hungary, what I would encourage them to—to do is ask themselves the question: not who's pro or anti-Europe, not who's pro or anti-the United States of America, but who is pro-you? Who is pro the people of Hungary? In my experience, I've seen a guy who has ferociously advocated for the interests of Hungary. I'm here to help him in this—in this campaign cycle. And yet when I sat down with Viktor, we didn't talk about politics. We talked about bah-bah, bah-bah, bah-bah, here are five things that we need, that the Hungarian people need from the United States in order to further our partnership and in order to achieve prosperity. That's the kind of leadership that is needed. And on everything from digital censorship, why are bureaucrats in Brussels telling social media companies what information they're giving to Hungarian voters? I think the voters of Hungary are adults. They are sovereign in their own country and they should be able to look at whatever information they would like to about the election without somebody in a far-away capital treating them like children. Sovereignty and democracy are fundamentally about the people choosing. And part of the reason why we're here and part of the reason why the President of the United States sent me here is because that we think the amount of interference that's come from the bureaucracy in Brussels has been truly disgraceful. I won't tell the people of Hungary how to vote, I would encourage the bureaucrats in Brussels to do the exact same thing. So Viktor, thank you and it's good to see you. Thank you Mr. Vice President. We have time for a couple of questions. The first two go to the Hungarian side and then the floor is yours Mr. Vice President. So the first question goes to Hungarian television, Csaba Yo. Thank you very much and good afternoon. I would not like to stand up because of the cameras. Thank you, I have two questions, one is to Mr. Prime Minister and the other one is to Mr. Vice President. From the Prime Minister I would like to ask if you did touch upon the possibilities of ending the Russian-Ukrainian war during the—your negotiations. And from the Vice President I would like to ask you to comment on the threats of President Zelensky towards Hungary and personally towards Viktor Orbán. Thank you. We did touch upon the Russian-Ukrainian war which is a painful subject. We're talking about a war waged between two Christian countries. Moreover, in the territory of Europe. So these two sentences actually set out how serious this war is. And I have always—and I've always really looked up upon the President of the United States. I'm talking about the current president obviously. That from the first moment onward he regarded these two dimensions as most important. In Europe two Orthodox deeply Christian countries are waging a war where tens and hundreds of thousands of people die and become injured for life. This is such—so terrible that you have to stop it at all costs. And since the United States prior to President Trump was in favor of this war, for us the current position of the United States is indeed very valuable because it is fundamentally pro-peace. So if a Hungarian and a US politician meet they cannot avoid talking about the Russian-Ukrainian war. Moreover, this war is being waged in the neighborhood of Hungary. Hungarians also die in this war.
